    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11544835176663148390">In the rush of modern life, we tend to lose touch with the peace that is available in each moment. World-renowned Zen master, spiritual leader, and author Thich Nhat Hanh shows us how to make positive use of the very situations that usually pressure and antagonize us. For him a ringing telephone can be a signal to call us back to our true selves. Dirty dishes, red lights, </span>
  <span id="freeText11544835176663148390" style="display:none">In the rush of modern life, we tend to lose touch with the peace that is available in each moment. World-renowned Zen master, spiritual leader, and author Thich Nhat Hanh shows us how to make positive use of the very situations that usually pressure and antagonize us. For him a ringing telephone can be a signal to call us back to our true selves. Dirty dishes, red lights, and traffic jams are spiritual friends on the path to "mindfulness"—the process of keeping our consciousness alive to our present experience and reality. The most profound satisfactions, the deepest feelings of joy and completeness lie as close at hand as our next aware breath and the smile we can form right now.<br /><br />Lucidly and beautifully written, <b>Peace Is Every Step </b>contains commentaries and meditations, personal anecdotes and stories from Nhat Hanh's experiences as a peace activist, teacher, and community leader. It begins where the reader already is—in the kitchen, office, driving a car, walking a part—and shows how deep meditative presence is available now. Nhat Hanh provides exercises to increase our awareness of our own body and mind through conscious breathing, which can bring immediate joy and peace. Nhat Hanh also shows how to be aware of relationships with others and of the world around us, its beauty and also its pollution and injustices. the deceptively simple practices of <b>Peace Is Every Step</b> encourage the reader to work for peace in the world as he or she continues to work on sustaining inner peace by turning the "mindless" into the mindFUL.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11544835176663148390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/278462-goodreads-quotes-walk-as-if-you-are">Goodreads quotes: &quot;walk as if you are kissing the earth with your feet&quot; - from this book. Couple of questions: 
(1) how? kissing and walking don&#39;t seem even remotely analogous activities; and 
(2) why? - it would seem a rather affected, not to say awkward, manner of walking even if one could work out how to do it - would it be ok to walk normally, while being mindfully appreciative of the earth on which you do so?</a>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2548177129" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2548177129" />
    <a title="Fergus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70395042-fergus"><img alt="Fergus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567548184p2/70395042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2548177129?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fergus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fergus" href="/user/show/70395042-fergus">Fergus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2548177129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6433782756030138478">One spectacular autumn day about twenty years ago, my wife and I departed from the awesome Saguenay valley for the long trip back to Ontario, by Greyhound coach.<br/><br/>We had been visiting my mother-in-law, who was then living in a seniors’ home. I remember well that my brother-in-law had made the faux pas of dropping us off at the city bus depot instead of the Greyhound stop.<br/><br/>Boy, did we have to scramble...<br/><br/>But we made it with time to spare! <br/><br/>Once seated in that high coach, as we went our long, fascinate</span>
  <span id="freeText6433782756030138478" style="display:none">One spectacular autumn day about twenty years ago, my wife and I departed from the awesome Saguenay valley for the long trip back to Ontario, by Greyhound coach.<br /><br />We had been visiting my mother-in-law, who was then living in a seniors’ home. I remember well that my brother-in-law had made the faux pas of dropping us off at the city bus depot instead of the Greyhound stop.<br /><br />Boy, did we have to scramble...<br /><br />But we made it with time to spare! <br /><br />Once seated in that high coach, as we went our long, fascinated way through that spectacular region of the Canadian Shield, a line of Mallarme came to me, as we passed beneath the endless ranks of towering evergreens:<br /><br />“Already it is the Home of all our True Groves!”<br /><br />You see, this primitive splendour was much like the Heaven of C.S. Lewis’ The Great Divorce, for Peace had descended over me like a sudden benediction.<br /><br />And it stuck around that day.<br /><br />And this book, too, is all about finding Peace.<br /><br />A peace that’s so deucedly difficult to find in this harried, mixed-up world of ours. Yes, that faraway lucky day I found it - and you can too!<br /><br />So thank you, my dear and gentle friend from over on the other, war-torn side of the twentieth century world...<br /><br />Only today have I remembered how I savoured your hopeful words in this book so many years ago.<br /><br />But with those wonderful memories there springs up the bitter taste of the hard and unforgiving workaday world I daily inhabited at that time.<br /><br />And as the noise of that world rose to a deafening crescendo, I turned - and this will sound strange to your saintly ears - to the comfort of an old-fashioned duality, in my former traditional faith.<br /><br />That will sound ominous to someone like you, in your nondual and nonjudgemental world!<br /><br />But I was getting old and cranky, and I saw that the very real harm that people were doing to each other was growing, not shrinking.<br /><br />You see, my quiet friend, there seemed no recourse for me to combat Evil other than with the Goodness of God. As plainly and obviously as I could - with all my heart AND mind!<br /><br />And your views were too gently vague for that. <br /><br />You see, ours is such an hard, ironclad world, and this world WINKS at Evil.<br /><br />Yet I offer to you today my heartfelt thanks for showing me the beginnings of the Way of the Spirit...<br /><br />Please know that, now that I am an old man, we aged somewhat similarly. My feeble muscles mimic your peaceful gestures, and my illusions, like yours, have all but disappeared.<br /><br />And now you have gone, and I can look a bit further along in my life, and see the quiet radiance of Eternity not much farther ahead of me!<br /><br />It has been a long road.<br /><br />And it was worth it, though for you it came after the simple stubbornness of lifelong forbearance, humility and service. But for undisciplined me, it comes now after a hard lifelong struggle to do the right thing in a mixed-up world.<br /><br />It was - yes, you’re right - a struggle against myself!<br /><br />But nature and God have done their work, and have nearly worn out my self out in spite of myself. But I have yet to learn to listen at all times to that still, quiet voice within.<br /><br />So go in peace, my friend.<br /><br />You did your work well.<br /><br />You gave the world - and me - the Hope of Peace in place of the world’s Endless Violent Rage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6433782756030138478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_418475564" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/418475564" />
    <a title="Kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5974610-kris"><img alt="Kris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390152276p2/5974610.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/418475564?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kris" href="/user/show/5974610-kris">Kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5974610-kris?shelf=buddhism">buddhism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5974610-kris?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5974610-kris?shelf=meditation">meditation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5974610-kris?shelf=religion-spirituality">religion-spirituality</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer418475564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18056513128401924336"><span>[image error]</span><br/><br/>Thich Nhat Hanh is a man who has lived his principles. Exiled from his native Vietnam for his active engagement in the peace movement as a Buddhist monk, he has lived in exile in France for years. He has an extraordinary bibliography of spiritual writing, from slim books to guide meditation to a length biography of the Buddha. <br/><br/>I am not certain he would thank me for providing that short biography. I think he would have preferred for me to start with a focus on the breath, on a gentle</span>
  <span id="freeText18056513128401924336" style="display:none"><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Thich Nhat Hanh is a man who has lived his principles. Exiled from his native Vietnam for his active engagement in the peace movement as a Buddhist monk, he has lived in exile in France for years. He has an extraordinary bibliography of spiritual writing, from slim books to guide meditation to a length biography of the Buddha. <br><br>I am not certain he would thank me for providing that short biography. I think he would have preferred for me to start with a focus on the breath, on a gentle step, on the clear sound of a bell, on a dahlia waving in breeze, on an oak tree's cool shade. <br><br>I started to read his writings because of my efforts to employ mindfulness meditation to deal with anxiety and fear. I took a course based on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8750.Jon_Kabat_Zinn" title="Jon Kabat-Zinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Jon Kabat-Zinn</a>'s UMass program described in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8157069.Full_Catastrophe_Living_Using_the_Wisdom_of_Your_Body_and_Mind_to_Face_Stress__Pain__and_Illness" title="Full Catastrophe Living Using the Wisdom of Your Body and Mind to Face Stress, Pain, and Illness by Jon Kabat-Zinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Full Catastrophe Living: Using the Wisdom of Your Body and Mind to Face Stress, Pain, and Illness</a>. For a while, like so many others, I was struggling with anxiety -- shortness of breath, catastrophic thinking, heart palpitations, the full gamut of fight or flight reactions. Mindfulness meditation helped me to slow down, to focus on the present, to sit with fear until it left of its own accord. <br><br>However, out of the structure of a weekly class, it can be extremely difficult to keep up the practice. It is all to easy to let life interfere. So, earlier this week I picked up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14572.Peace_Is_Every_Step_The_Path_of_Mindfulness_in_Everyday_Life" title="Peace Is Every Step The Path of Mindfulness in Everyday Life by Thich Nhat Hanh" rel="nofollow noopener">Peace Is Every Step: The Path of Mindfulness in Everyday Life</a> and started to read it throughout the week. And as i hoped, it helped me to tap into that center of calm when I most needed to do so.<br><br>The volume is divided into three sections: "Breathe! You Are Alive," which presents mindfulness principles in the context of everyday life in the West; "Transformation and Healing," which drew my attention in this reading for Thich Nhat Hanh's gentle and insightful discussion of how to best deal with destructive emotions through meditation; and "Peace is Every Step," in which he provides an overview of how we can all approach peace work with help from meditation.<br><br>This is an excellent book for novice meditators. It is not written with an assumption that the reader is a practicing Buddhist or has practiced much meditation. The chapters are very short, often just a page or two, so they can be read as devotional texts anchoring the reader in her day. And his tone throughout is gentle and encouraging, even as Thich Nhat Hanh addresses some difficult topics:<br><br>"Mindful observation is based on the principle of 'non-duality': our feeling is not separate from us or caused merely by something outside us; our feeling is us, and for that moment, we are that feeling. We are neither drowned nor terrorized by the feeling, nor do we reject it. Our attitude of not clinging to or rejecting our feelings is the attitude of letting go, an important part of meditation practice." (62)<br><br>"Our conscious, reasoning mind knows that negative feelings such as anger, fear, &amp; regret are not wholly acceptable to ourselves or society, so it finds ways to repress them, to push them into remote areas of our consciousness in order to forget them. Because we want to avoid suffering, we create defense mechanisms that deny the existence of these negative feelings &amp; give us the impression we have peace within ourselves. But our internal formations are always looking for ways to manifest as destructive images, feelings, thoughts, words, or behavior." (78)<br><br>Thich Nhat Hanh also provides some humorous passages:<br>"Some of us may prefer to go into our room, lock the door, and punch a pillow. We call this 'getting in touch with our anger." But I don't think this is getting in touch with our anger at all. In fact, I don't think it is even getting in touch with our pillow. If we are really in touch with the pillow, we know what a pillow is and we won't hit it." (71)<br><br>In the end, this is a book that acknowledges the many challenges and sorrows in life, but draws our attention to the power of the present, the everyday, the real, in the midst of the phantoms of yesterday and tomorrow that plague us. This is a book that is diffused with hope, compassion and love:<br>“Hope is important because it can make the present moment less difficult to bear. If we believe that tomorrow will be better, we can bear a hardship today.” <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18056513128401924336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18314531536368549316" style="display:none">I first read this book in college, when my friend Maran told me it was her favorite book ever. It's a little book, and I finished it quickly, and while I really liked it, not much of it stuck with me. It wasn't until I read it again that I realized how genius it really is. I'm never going to be a Buddhist monk, or even a proper Buddhist, but Thich Nhat Hanh talks about slowing down, connecting with the moment, and how to deal with stress and negative emotions in such a loving, gentle way that it feels like anyone could do it.</span>

  <span id="freeText594693477209878702" style="display:none">'when you plant lettuce, if it does not grow well, you don't blame the lettuce. you look into the reasons it is not doing well. it may need fertilizer, or more water, or less sun. you never blame the lettuce. yet if we have problems with our friends or our family, we blame the other person. but if we know how to take care of them, they will grow well, like lettuce. blaming has no positive effect at all, nor does trying to persuade using reason and arguments. that is my experience. no blame, no reasoning, nor arguments, just understanding. if you understand, and you show that you understand, you can love, and the situation will change.'<br /><br />thich nhat hanh<br />peace is every step<br /><br /><br />i read this book about a thousand years ago, and then the other day a friend of mine gave me the most wonderful gift-- she handed me this book, my own book, from my own shelf. it can look and read like something a little embarrassing-- an easy self-help manual, or treacly pop buddhism. i can't answer this except to say, somewhat vaguely, that this is that rarest thing-- a simple book that rewards multiple readings. while a first reading may provide a facile sense of revelation, i suppose that the only real transformative power comes with simple repetition (which is only to be expected, given the central role of simple repetition in buddhist pratice, as i understand it).</span>

<div id="review_8067651" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8067651" />
    <a title="Chanita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/546603-chanita"><img alt="Chanita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386431924p2/546603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8067651?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chanita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chanita" href="/user/show/546603-chanita">Chanita</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/546603-chanita?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/546603-chanita?shelf=spirituality">spirituality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/546603-chanita?shelf=to-read-own">to-read-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/546603-chanita?shelf=buddhism">buddhism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8067651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1633883356031999556">Thich Nhat Hanh's writing is deceptive in its subtlety. He'll go on and on with stories about tree-hugging or metaphors involving raw potatoes; he'll tell you how to eat mindfully, even how to breathe and walk; he'll suggest looking closely at a flower and to see the sun as your heart. As the Zen teacher Richard Baker commented, however, Nhat Hanh is "a cross between a cloud, a snail, and piece of heavy machinery." Sooner or later, it begins to sink in that Nhat Hanh is conveying a depth of psyc</span>
  <span id="freeText1633883356031999556" style="display:none">Thich Nhat Hanh's writing is deceptive in its subtlety. He'll go on and on with stories about tree-hugging or metaphors involving raw potatoes; he'll tell you how to eat mindfully, even how to breathe and walk; he'll suggest looking closely at a flower and to see the sun as your heart. As the Zen teacher Richard Baker commented, however, Nhat Hanh is "a cross between a cloud, a snail, and piece of heavy machinery." Sooner or later, it begins to sink in that Nhat Hanh is conveying a depth of psychology and a world outlook that require nothing less than a complete paradigm shift. Through his cute stories and compassionate admonitions, he gradually builds up to his philosophy of interbeing, the notion that none of us is separately, but rather that we inter-are. The ramifications are explosive. How can we mindlessly and selfishly pursue our individual ends, when we are inextricably bound up with everyone and everything else? We see an enemy not as focus of anger but as a human with a complex history, who could be us if we had the same history. Suffice it to say, that after reading Peace Is Every Step, you'll never look at a plastic bag the same way again, and you may even develop a penchant for hugging trees. --Brian Bruya<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1633883356031999556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90098391" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90098391" />
    <a title="PlatKat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/359130-platkat"><img alt="PlatKat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1189180079p2/359130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90098391?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PlatKat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PlatKat" href="/user/show/359130-platkat">PlatKat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to PlatKat by: </span>
      My old boss from back in the day
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90098391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9563362514596161011">This book is full of beneficial guidelines for living a mindful, peaceful life and helping those around you do the same. Even if it confirms what you already know, it is a pleasurable read and a beautiful inspiration to actively appreciate the positive aspects of living.<br/><br/>Like most other Buddhist works, it is centered around living in the present. I wasn't expecting him to devote a section to the idea of hope as an obstacle, but it made good sense. It's very easy to keep looking toward tomorrow, w</span>
  <span id="freeText9563362514596161011" style="display:none">This book is full of beneficial guidelines for living a mindful, peaceful life and helping those around you do the same. Even if it confirms what you already know, it is a pleasurable read and a beautiful inspiration to actively appreciate the positive aspects of living.<br /><br />Like most other Buddhist works, it is centered around living in the present. I wasn't expecting him to devote a section to the idea of hope as an obstacle, but it made good sense. It's very easy to keep looking toward tomorrow, wishing for better days, but in doing that you're practicing avoidance. Facing your current situation and dealing with it head-on isn't always easy, but it's heavily encouraged here.<br /><br />I also appreciated Thich Nhat Hanh's encouragement to eliminate distractions. We waste so much time being "entertained" that we forget to live our own lives to the fullest. Not being a fan of most television programming myself, I am all for turning off the TV and foregoing the 40,000 some-odd murders we see a year, the 80,000 or so companies shoving products and services in our faces that we must "buy now," and the made-up numbers I use to talk about these unnecessary absurdities.<br /><br />What's more dangerous than violence and guerrilla advertising, I think, is what we neglect when we decide we'd rather be entertained than really alive. When we fall into the fantasy worlds TV, games, and online environments provide, we are putting aside the important people who comprise our actual worlds. If you have 30 minutes to kill, why not take a walk or write a letter to someone you haven't seen in awhile? Even if you're dirt poor and in the middle of nowhere, you can still meditate. It'll clear out your mind and improve your mood over whatever the latest reality show is pushing.<br /><br />Another main point of this book is to deepen your understanding of your friends and enemies alike. And then, it's not enough to just understand, you have to act on this understanding. In order to reconcile your differences, you have to talk to the other person to test your real strength. Having the peace of mind to do this in a calm, well-executed fashion is tough, but when you come upon challenges like this, it is comforting to have this simple yet powerful book to lay the framework for some good meditation sessions.<br /><br />"Peace Is Every Step" came at a good time for me. At this point in my life where everything seems to be in upheaval, it's nice to remember that I can decide to be centered whenever I want. I need not depend on outside circumstances or other people to relax and find my own true happiness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9563362514596161011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2585800482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2585800482" />
    <a title="Hákon Gunnarsson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson"><img alt="Hákon Gunnarsson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474574814p2/20498454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2585800482?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hákon Gunnarsson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hákon Gunnarsson" href="/user/show/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson">Hákon Gunnarsson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson?shelf=buddhism">buddhism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson?shelf=meditation">meditation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson?shelf=mindfulness">mindfulness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2585800482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6064088551635456927">This is the second Thich Nhat Hanh book I read in a a month, and I have to say I like his writing. This book is a bit simpler than the one I read last. It doesn’t cover as much ground, but what it does cover, it does so beautifully.<br/><br/>He talks about his view of life, activism, and Buddhism without being overly preachy. And he also talks about his life, and he has lead an interesting one. Because of his work during the Vietnam war he can’t go back to his native country. It seems that because he and </span>
  <span id="freeText6064088551635456927" style="display:none">This is the second Thich Nhat Hanh book I read in a a month, and I have to say I like his writing. This book is a bit simpler than the one I read last. It doesn’t cover as much ground, but what it does cover, it does so beautifully.<br /><br />He talks about his view of life, activism, and Buddhism without being overly preachy. And he also talks about his life, and he has lead an interesting one. Because of his work during the Vietnam war he can’t go back to his native country. It seems that because he and his followers didn’t take sides during the war they got into trouble with both sides. <br /><br />Peace is every step is an idea that is central to his views on life. Peace and mindfulness isn’t something to do just at a specific place, but rather something to keep with you at all times, in every step. <br /><br />When he started to talk about anger, and how that can rule a person, I couldn’t help thinking about the news that we are bombarded with every day. There are so many people that let anger, and hate do their driving, too many resorting to killing because of it. How much of it, is their anger, and how much of it is inherited? However a person gets to the point of letting their anger do the driving, it too often ends up making things even worse. <br /><br />In short, this book is not that heavy on Buddhism. It centers more around mindfulness, and how to find it. There are times when he paint a little bit too rosy picture for me, but most of the time I just think what he says is beautiful, and I think he does have a point about a lot of things. I really liked it. I’d recommend it to anyone that is interested in mindfulness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6064088551635456927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_29681005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29681005" />
    <a title="Maureen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1180394-maureen"><img alt="Maureen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1214579372p2/1180394.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29681005?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/1180394-maureen">Maureen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Maureen by: </span>
      Parallax Press
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1180394-maureen?shelf=buddhism">buddhism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29681005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10414943841734211328">Some of Thich Nhat Hanh's writings are mostly informational, like <i>Old Path, White Clouds</i>, his biography of the Buddha. Others, like this book, are meant to be experienced. <br/><br/>In each short section of this book, Thich Nhat Hanh tells a story, or seeks to describe an experience to which the reader may relate. Some of them, like washing the dishes, deal with being in the present moment, and being deeply involved in whatever one is doing solely for the joy of having that experience. Others, like his de</span>
  <span id="freeText10414943841734211328" style="display:none">Some of Thich Nhat Hanh's writings are mostly informational, like <i>Old Path, White Clouds</i>, his biography of the Buddha. Others, like this book, are meant to be experienced. <br /><br />In each short section of this book, Thich Nhat Hanh tells a story, or seeks to describe an experience to which the reader may relate. Some of them, like washing the dishes, deal with being in the present moment, and being deeply involved in whatever one is doing solely for the joy of having that experience. Others, like his descriptions of a sheet of paper or eating a tangerine, show the interconnectedness of life. In the case of the sheet of paper, the sun, the rain, the tree, the man who cut the tree down, and other factors go into the making of the paper. Without the "non-paper" elements, the paper would not be.<br /><br />Contemplation of a tangerine is another favorite: one day Thich Nhat Hanh gave some children tangerines. They contemplated not just the fruit in their hands, but also its mother, the tree that bore the fruit. Then they visualized the blossoms in the sunshine and the rain, and the growth of the tiny fruit. Then the children were invited to peel the tangerine, taking in the sensations of the spray of the mist from the peel, the smell of the fruit, and its texture. Finally, they were invited to taste it.<br /><br />I have eaten a tangerine with Thich Nhat Hanh, and if the exercise is entered into sincerely, it is a mind-blowing experience. To think that this man who has such a deep reverence for the simplest things of life has also endured the self-immolation of his brothers in the Order of Interbeing in protest of the war in his homeland, the tragedy of the Vietnamese boat people, and life for so many years in exile, brings an almost unendurable sorrow. <br /><br />And yet, the tangerine remains.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10414943841734211328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review29681005">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1036457226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036457226" />
    <a title="Max" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7347257-max"><img alt="Max" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1036457226?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Max" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Max" href="/user/show/7347257-max">Max</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1036457226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9517131229754115516">In the beginning of my studying of Buddhism, I quickly came to appreciate Hanh as a wise Buddhist Monk. I've watched many of his video interviews and lectures. This was the first book of his that I read. I was excited at first to begin reading and learning, but quickly I realized that this wasn't the book for me. It's too simplistic, and not in a good way. Although some might say that over complicating peace and mindfulness is exactly what Hanh would advise against, I would argue that some conte</span>
  <span id="freeText9517131229754115516" style="display:none">In the beginning of my studying of Buddhism, I quickly came to appreciate Hanh as a wise Buddhist Monk. I've watched many of his video interviews and lectures. This was the first book of his that I read. I was excited at first to begin reading and learning, but quickly I realized that this wasn't the book for me. It's too simplistic, and not in a good way. Although some might say that over complicating peace and mindfulness is exactly what Hanh would advise against, I would argue that some content needs to be expanded upon, rather than narrated as though this is a children's book. His silly metaphors and examples of speaking to inanimate objects just didn't appeal to me. If you have any prior knowledge of Buddha's teachings, you will likely not learn much from this book.<br />It's difficult to give this book a numerical rating, since it probably means different things to different people.<br />Perhaps if you are experiencing a particularly difficult time in your life, or you're being challenged with stressful situations, this book could help guide you towards inner peace. In which case this book is 4 stars.<br /><br />If you're like me and you're seeking to learn more about Buddhism or Hanh's teachings beyond the most basic theories of mindfulness, this book may be not be for you. In which case this book is 1 star.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9517131229754115516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1835645171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1835645171" />
    <a title="Gauri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3760321-gauri"><img alt="Gauri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532650487p2/3760321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1835645171?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gauri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gauri" href="/user/show/3760321-gauri">Gauri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3760321-gauri?shelf=most-meaningful">most-meaningful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3760321-gauri?shelf=depression">depression</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1835645171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13174982413973428125">Hanh is a Vietnamese Buddhist monk who led the effort towards peace during the Vietnam war, and has worked for many years in other countries to help refugees and to spread his philosophy of peace. In this book, he speaks about the individual's journey towards inner peace. He maintains that to achieve peace around the world, individuals themselves must achieve inner peace, because peace is not something you can will to exist or force on others, but is rather, a collective understanding of one ano</span>
  <span id="freeText13174982413973428125" style="display:none">Hanh is a Vietnamese Buddhist monk who led the effort towards peace during the Vietnam war, and has worked for many years in other countries to help refugees and to spread his philosophy of peace. In this book, he speaks about the individual's journey towards inner peace. He maintains that to achieve peace around the world, individuals themselves must achieve inner peace, because peace is not something you can will to exist or force on others, but is rather, a collective understanding of one another in societies and between societies. This philosophy reminds me of Rumi's quote, "Yesterday I was clever, so I wanted to change the world; today I am wise, so I am changing myself." This is a quote I have lived by for a couple of years now, and the depth of this quote has now become much greater through my knowledge of Hanh's philosophy. <br />The first part of this book discusses the the basics of meditation and what mindfulness is. Meditation is not actually just the act of sitting down and concentrating on one's breath, but can also be being aware of oneself throughout the day and being aware of the details around oneself. Breathing is a method to be aware of oneself, and by practicing conscious breathing during parts of the day, you can know that you are truly in the present and the world is truly here. Appreciation starts in the present. <br />The second part of the book discusses how this practice can be used during intensely emotional or violent situations, either within yourself of between others. The version of me from a year ago would've been resentful towards Hanh's writing, insisting that no one can demand this sort of behavior from me if the rest of the world is so terrible. But now, I understand. No one is demanding this out of me. I behave peacefully and become peaceful to take care of my own mind and self and to not torture myself with ill feelings. As for the rest of the world, how I deal with conflict and how I impact others can be improved through my peaceful behavior. <br />The third part of the book discusses the interconnected-ness of a human being to other human beings and other aspects of the world. To read this book, I depended on a publishing house to develop this ink on this paper. To get this paper, I depended on a logger to cut a tree. To have that tree, I depended on the soil, the clouds, and the Sun. In addition, the crime of others are not entirely their fault; though they must accept the responsibility of their actions, we must also realize that society had a role in cultivating such violence. The wealth of others does mean the poverty of the rest. <br />Ultimately, I am very, very glad that someone recommended this book to me. This has given me so much to work with everyday. As a young person, I seek to shape my mind to understand the complexities and nuances of the world and understand myself and my actions. I now would like to learn more about mindfulness, meditation, and Buddhism. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13174982413973428125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2095474771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1082636421408007788">A book that I think would make a difference in our modern day civilization if only more people would read it. It is a book of reminders, but not just any reminders, fundamental and essential reminders. We are reminded to breathe deeply and learn to be at peace and experience joy with the present moment. We are reminded of how many of our lives are overflowing with blessings that could easily make us weep in appreciation and gratefulness. We have food, we still have some Nature around us (we shou</span>
  <span id="freeText1082636421408007788" style="display:none">A book that I think would make a difference in our modern day civilization if only more people would read it. It is a book of reminders, but not just any reminders, fundamental and essential reminders. We are reminded to breathe deeply and learn to be at peace and experience joy with the present moment. We are reminded of how many of our lives are overflowing with blessings that could easily make us weep in appreciation and gratefulness. We have food, we still have some Nature around us (we should definitely work to take a much deeper care of her), some of us have family close to us, and many other treasures that we usually forget to value as such in our daily lives. By remembering to stop and having a look at all of these amazing blessings, our lives improve dramatically, no pay raise involved, no new sports car needed, or no fancy jewelry required. The key to happiness, and therefore to collective peace, then, is simply creating a daily habit of breathing and noticing how fortunate we are. From this we will also garner the strength needed to face our daily challenges. This is the gift that this book gave me.</span>

I love this book so much that I plan on buying several copies for all of my family members to read. Get ready to be transformed!</span>

<div id="review_101875695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101875695" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1887726-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231526829p2/1887726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101875695?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1887726-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101875695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12469518587340263240">I loved this gem of a book. Each tiny chapter give you something to reflect upon for weeks. It is about finding peace and happiness in your life and sharing that with the world. He talks about the importance of mindfulness so you can be aware of your inter-relatedness in the entire universe. This book was a Mother's Day gift one year ago and it added greater peace and understanding to my life. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10813238542711875122">A beautiful little book, this is.<br/><br/>Few people would argue if you told them life feels like chaos sometimes. Or maybe all the time. Stopping to breathe and find peace is, in today’s world, almost unheard of. Particularly in our lovely little over-caffeinated, double-booked, mindless-drone American society, slowing down is practically Original Sin (because everyone knows that lunch breaks and adequate sleep predicated the fall of mankind, duh).<br/><br/>But why do this to ourselves? And, ultimately, to each o</span>
  <span id="freeText10813238542711875122" style="display:none">A beautiful little book, this is.<br /><br />Few people would argue if you told them life feels like chaos sometimes. Or maybe all the time. Stopping to breathe and find peace is, in today’s world, almost unheard of. Particularly in our lovely little over-caffeinated, double-booked, mindless-drone American society, slowing down is practically Original Sin (because everyone knows that lunch breaks and adequate sleep predicated the fall of mankind, duh).<br /><br />But why do this to ourselves? And, ultimately, to each other? And to the planet that we call home? <br /><br />I’m no guru, but I can tell you that a thoroughly oxygenated, centered Sarah feels quite a bit better than a so-insanely-anxious-and-insecure-that-I-can-barely-function Sarah. A little focus on my breath to calm that cyclone is well worth the price of a few minutes. And actually, as it turns out, that calm, quiet, set-aside time is LITERAL BLISS. Who knew?!<br /><br />There’s a bonus, too. When I breathe and find peace, I’m able to be a better human creature, a better social worker, and a better me. (Shocking that all this is shocking, by the way).<br /><br />Doing and being good in this world takes presence of mind and a steadfast sense of interconnectedness (inter-being, as it were). Thich Nhat Hanh tells us that this is all possible if we take a minute to slow our roll, inhale some air, and reacquaint ourselves with beautiful, terrifying, oh-so-vast Reality. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10813238542711875122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_619484823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619484823" />
    <a title="♥ Ibrahim ♥ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1178748-ibrahim"><img alt="♥ Ibrahim ♥ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557598809p2/1178748.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619484823?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ Ibrahim ♥ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ Ibrahim ♥ " href="/user/show/1178748-ibrahim">♥ Ibrahim ♥ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1178748-ibrahim?shelf=thinkers-i-adore">thinkers-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1178748-ibrahim?shelf=spirituality">spirituality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1178748-ibrahim?shelf=writing">writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619484823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12529415111716558293"><br/>Originally I heard about this book from another author that I was really, still am, enjoying her book "writing begins with the breath" by Laraine Herring. I was pleased to know that in reading this book I will get some skills in towards enhancing my writing, some skills in mindfulness and some skills so that I may grow as a Christian and human being in my development journey. First thing that struck me about this book was what Thomas Merton had to say about Thây (Thich). He told his students, "J</span>
  <span id="freeText12529415111716558293" style="display:none"><br />Originally I heard about this book from another author that I was really, still am, enjoying her book "writing begins with the breath" by Laraine Herring. I was pleased to know that in reading this book I will get some skills in towards enhancing my writing, some skills in mindfulness and some skills so that I may grow as a Christian and human being in my development journey. First thing that struck me about this book was what Thomas Merton had to say about Thây (Thich). He told his students, "Just the way he opens the door and enters a room demonstrates his understanding. He is a true monk." I couldn't help but notice how young, peaceful this man, Thây, looked. What can these Buddhists teach me about peace? Peace and happiness are available if I can only quiet my distracted thinking long enough to come back to the present moment and notice the blue sky, the child's smile, the beautiful sunrise. The book is simply teaching me how to just live, and live in the present moment. I only need to be awake, alive in the present moment. There are no amount of things I can pile up in order to acquire peace and happiness as they are both mine to claim now. What better way to start the day than with a smile? My smile here affirms my determination and awareness to live in peace and joy. The source of a true smile is an awakened mind. A smile will relax all the muscles in my face; it will banish all worries and fatigue. There is no better gift to give to our family as well as people overall than the gift our awareness, our smile. Then he teaches me a number of breathing techniques. As I breathe in, I say to myself, "Breathing in, I know that I am breathing in." And as I breathe out, I say, "breathing out, I know that I am breathing out.". Just that. Breathing in is my in-breath and breathing out is my out-breath. I don't have to repeat the whole sentence; I can just use two words, "In" and "Out". Sometimes my mind is thinking of one thing and my body is doing another, and this would mean that mind and body are not unified. My goal is to bring them together, and become whole again. Breathing in, I calm my body. Breathing out, I smile. My appointment with life is in the present moment, hence, peace is every step of the way. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12529415111716558293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_220058992" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/220058992" />
    <a title="Arizona Mildman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6576934-arizona-mildman"><img alt="Arizona Mildman" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/220058992?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arizona Mildman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arizona Mildman" href="/user/show/6576934-arizona-mildman">Arizona Mildman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220058992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17129024594801970418">Thich Nhat Hanh writes this as if we were completely without any knowledge of Buddhism. He could have called it Simple Meditation Made Easy. I have studied meditation and it is normally taught by people who complicate the process so they can teach you the "proper" way to do it. Hanh teaches that simple breathing is the key. He teaches mindfulness in walking, driving, housework, any occasion and makes it so simple anyone, including me can follow and successfully be enjoying deep meditation by the</span>
  <span id="freeText17129024594801970418" style="display:none">Thich Nhat Hanh writes this as if we were completely without any knowledge of Buddhism. He could have called it Simple Meditation Made Easy. I have studied meditation and it is normally taught by people who complicate the process so they can teach you the "proper" way to do it. Hanh teaches that simple breathing is the key. He teaches mindfulness in walking, driving, housework, any occasion and makes it so simple anyone, including me can follow and successfully be enjoying deep meditation by the end of the book in as long as it takes you to read and practice about 40 minutes a day. It slows down your breathing and thinking and allows you to successfully stop mindless thought that are the seeds of good and bad and helps us decide how to unlock the use of the right way. One who has studied Buddhism for years gets as much out of this book because without the complicated mythology and confusing behavior taught by some dharma teachers, one gets to hear the dharma in a way that ultimately made more sense to me in a few hours than I had learned in years of study with some teachers. Basing all of his works on the four noble truths and the eightfold path, one can't really go wrong in absorbing all of Thich Nhat Hanh's writings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17129024594801970418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText12826342457593449436" style="display:none">I picked up this book after being impressed by Thich Nhat Hanh's podcast on breathing. <div id="review_96801419" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96801419" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1064222-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384742259p2/1064222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96801419?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/1064222-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rebecca by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1389263-holly">Holly</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1064222-rebecca?shelf=asian">asian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1064222-rebecca?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96801419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17570984634765513068"><br/>I have always been a proponent for breathing.<br/><br/>No, seriously.<br/><br/>I have had bouts with allergies and asthma and have felt the terror of gasping for a breath ... but I have also had experience with meditation, self-relaxation and deep breathing (I delivered my second child using the 'Hypno-birthing' method). Conscious breathing can be powerful.<br/><br/><blockquote><i>Breathing in and out is very important, and it is enjoyable. Our breathing is the link between our body and our mind... Just breathing and smiling can make us ve</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText17570984634765513068" style="display:none"><br />I have always been a proponent for breathing.<br /><br />No, seriously.<br /><br />I have had bouts with allergies and asthma and have felt the terror of gasping for a breath ... but I have also had experience with meditation, self-relaxation and deep breathing (I delivered my second child using the 'Hypno-birthing' method). Conscious breathing can be powerful.<br /><br /><blockquote><i>Breathing in and out is very important, and it is enjoyable. Our breathing is the link between our body and our mind... Just breathing and smiling can make us very happy, because when we breath consciously we recover ourselves completely and encounter life in the present moment</i> (p. 9).</blockquote><br /><br />In this beautiful and simple treatise, Nhất Hạnh gently admonishes us to take time to stop and breath. By so doing, he teaches, we can find our own inner peace, provide ourselves with the understanding to bring peace to our family and community and, ultimately, find the compassion needed to heal the world. His is a message similar to Ghandi's: "<i>Be the change you want to see in the world"</i> or, "Before you can change the world, you have to change yourself."<br /><br />A few poignant excerpts:<br /><blockquote><i>When we are angry, we are not usually inclined to return to ourselves. We want to think about the person who is making us angry, to think about his hateful aspects - his rudeness, dishonesty, cruelty, maliciousness, and so on. The more we think about him, listen to him, or look at him, the more our anger flares. His dishonesty and hatefulness may be real, imaginary, or exaggerated, but, in fact, the root of the problem is the anger itself, and we have to come back and look first of all inside ourselves</i> (p. 57).</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>If we genuinely try to understand the suffering of another person, we are more likely to act in a way that will help him overcome his suffering and confusion, and that will help all of us</i> (p. 64).</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>Most of us want to take sides in each encounter or conflict. We distinguish right from wrong based on partial evidence or hearsay. We need indignation in order to act, but even righteous, legitimate indignation is not enough. Our world does not lack people willing to throw themselves into action. What we need are people who are capable of loving, of not taking sides so that they can embrace the whole of reality</i> (p. 120-21).</blockquote><br /><blockquote><i>When you first learn of something like that </i>[rape of a young girl by a pirate]<i>, you get angry at the pirate. You naturally take the side of the girl. As you look more deeply you will see it differently. If you take the side of the little girl, then it is easy. You only have to take a gun and shoot the pirate. But we cannot do that. In my meditation I saw that if I had been born in the village of the pirate and raised in the same conditions as he was, there is a great likelihood that I would become a pirate. I saw that many babies are born along the Gulf of Siam, hundreds every day, and if we educators, social workers, politicians, and others do not do something about the situation, in twenty-five years a number of them will become sea pirates. That is certain. If you or I were born today in those fishing villages, we may become sea pirates in twenty-five years. If you take a gun and shoot the pirate, you shoot all of us, because all of us are to some extent responsible for this state of affairs</i> (p. 122).</blockquote><br /><br />Nhất Hạnh's main message may sound naive. It may come across as an optimistic oversimplification of the overwhelming nature of the issues. But his message is a tangible and achievable start: <br />Solve world hunger, nuclear war and depletion of the rain forests! <br />Breathe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17570984634765513068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/983495685?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Azadeh Seif Amirhosseini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Azadeh Seif Amirhosseini" href="/user/show/32726693-azadeh-seif-amirhosseini">Azadeh Seif Amirhosseini</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer983495685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4692271493887234448">Browsing through Waterstones in London in July 2009, I came across Thich Nhat Hanh's, Peace is Every Step: The Path of Mindfulness in Everyday Life. At this time I was in a place in my life where many dreams and goals were becoming uncertain and life was beginning to become a little negative but all changed after reading this book.<br/> <br/>As I began to read through the first chapter, I was captivated by Thich Nhat Hanh's wisdom, writing style and language.<br/> <br/>Because of this wonderful book, I am learning </span>
  <span id="freeText4692271493887234448" style="display:none">Browsing through Waterstones in London in July 2009, I came across Thich Nhat Hanh's, Peace is Every Step: The Path of Mindfulness in Everyday Life. At this time I was in a place in my life where many dreams and goals were becoming uncertain and life was beginning to become a little negative but all changed after reading this book.<br /> <br />As I began to read through the first chapter, I was captivated by Thich Nhat Hanh's wisdom, writing style and language.<br /> <br />Because of this wonderful book, I am learning everyday in life that we as humans take so much for granted but should try and be grateful for all our blessings. When tears were rolling down reading each line of the first chapter, 5 years ago, I began to feel enlightened by Thich Nhat Hanh's buddhist mindfulness and philosophy. Realizing just how limited my perception of life can be, I was taught to take pleasure and peace from the most simple of everyday events such as washing the dishes or tidying the home, for even in the most simple chores, understanding, appreciation and mindfulness can arise, as Thich Nhat Hanh and the Buddha's teachings beautifully convey. <br /><br />Life is filled with many possibilities brimming to make the most of it, is a vital lesson I have gladly taken away with me in this book. <br /><br />Thank you Thich Nhat Hanh, for your writings and guidance gives me strength and inspiration, you are a life changing gentleman and author.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1143293542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1143293542" />
    <a title="Tanya Tosheva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5988627-tanya-tosheva"><img alt="Tanya Tosheva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492637056p2/5988627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1143293542?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya Tosheva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya Tosheva" href="/user/show/5988627-tanya-tosheva">Tanya Tosheva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5988627-tanya-tosheva?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1143293542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3587825090715530674">This is not a book I'd usually pick up. My curiosity often shifts from one topic to another and the last time it was engaged with Eastern philosophy and Buddhism (about a year and a half ago, I think) I was left with a deep certainty that it is not a philosophy I can ever truly accept. Life without craving or desire is not a life worth living, so why would anyone want it? I'm never going to be a person without desires and hopes and dreams that is content and happy just to sit on the grass and st</span>
  <span id="freeText3587825090715530674" style="display:none">This is not a book I'd usually pick up. My curiosity often shifts from one topic to another and the last time it was engaged with Eastern philosophy and Buddhism (about a year and a half ago, I think) I was left with a deep certainty that it is not a philosophy I can ever truly accept. Life without craving or desire is not a life worth living, so why would anyone want it? I'm never going to be a person without desires and hopes and dreams that is content and happy just to sit on the grass and stare at a flower, thank you very much.<br />Well, that hasn't changed. But you'd be hard-pressed to find a book I was more in need of reading than this one. The mindful living described in this book does not mean living with no desires. It means being able to detach yourself from the pain of the past, the worries about the future, the many <i>knots</i> of anger, disappointment, suspicion, hurt tied up inside you and just <i>be</i>. Enjoy the simple beauty of breathing, of seeing a painting that you like, of hearing a poem that you enjoy or eating a well-prepared meal. It's about learning to untie the knots and calm your fears. And accept that there can be no flowers without dirt and garbage. It's a book about attaining the peace of mind every single one of us needs from time to time.<br />There's a lot to learn from this book, even if you don't decide to throw away all your worldly possessions and go live in a hermitage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3587825090715530674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2424577664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2424577664" />
    <a title="sevdah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2890368-sevdah"><img alt="sevdah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556522366p2/2890368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2424577664?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sevdah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sevdah" href="/user/show/2890368-sevdah">sevdah</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2424577664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10095974629742196369">Ok listen. It is a book on mindfulness by a Buddhist monk who explains you need to breathe and smile as much as you can and your life will get better. And I mean I know we just don't have real time for this, and smiling isn't it at the moment. And it makes close to no sense. But then he starts expanding and building on the idea of noticing all your feelings, the way your body, mind, emotions are, just noticing them without trying to correct them or anything. Forget about breathing through your a</span>
  <span id="freeText10095974629742196369" style="display:none">Ok listen. It is a book on mindfulness by a Buddhist monk who explains you need to breathe and smile as much as you can and your life will get better. And I mean I know we just don't have real time for this, and smiling isn't it at the moment. And it makes close to no sense. But then he starts expanding and building on the idea of noticing all your feelings, the way your body, mind, emotions are, just noticing them without trying to correct them or anything. Forget about breathing through your anger - the goal here is to notice and accept it and do that over and over again until something cracks and you start seeing more deeply into it. And then he moves on how to use this kind of attention for other - to empathy, understanding, kindness, and imagines a world in which we all just collectively bring our consciousness to our breath many times a day and asks the question of what would happen if we all lived this way. And you know what, yeah, it might not sound very hip and I can't say if they'd still have flat white in that world, but it sounds so good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10095974629742196369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16671569888694119042">Aside from prayer and music, Thich Nhat Hanh is my go-to guy for finding that peaceful, still place in the center of the storm. This book is thin, easy to read, and practical. After explaining why it is important to live in the moment, and how breathing and meditation can assist with this, TNH provides several recipes -- for lack of a better word -- to try out, especially while taking a walk. Written for newbies, not experts, this book is handy and accessible.<br/><br/> I have read several of his books, i</span>
  <span id="freeText16671569888694119042" style="display:none">Aside from prayer and music, Thich Nhat Hanh is my go-to guy for finding that peaceful, still place in the center of the storm. This book is thin, easy to read, and practical. After explaining why it is important to live in the moment, and how breathing and meditation can assist with this, TNH provides several recipes -- for lack of a better word -- to try out, especially while taking a walk. Written for newbies, not experts, this book is handy and accessible.<br /><br /> I have read several of his books, including an interesting comparison between the teachings of the Christ and the teachings of the Buddha, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73184.Living_Buddha__Living_Christ" title="Living Buddha, Living Christ by Thich Nhat Hanh" rel="nofollow noopener">Living Buddha, Living Christ</a>, and a wonderful picture book for helping children overcome anger and fear, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/816226.A_Pebble_for_Your_Pocket" title="A Pebble for Your Pocket by Thich Nhat Hanh" rel="nofollow noopener">A Pebble for Your Pocket</a>. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7618831505592523252">Thich Nhat Hanh's Peace is Every Step is by far my favorite of all the books written by gurus and thinkers. This book has changed my perspective on my perspective. He has, through his compassionate and down-to-earth dialogue, allowed me to understand and be compassionate toward my own Catholic faith, myself, and everyone around me. <br/><br/>This isn't a book filled with buzzwords nor is it a book that preaches. Thich Nhat Hanh does not offer techniques or ideologies, he simply presents the world as it re</span>
  <span id="freeText7618831505592523252" style="display:none">Thich Nhat Hanh's Peace is Every Step is by far my favorite of all the books written by gurus and thinkers. This book has changed my perspective on my perspective. He has, through his compassionate and down-to-earth dialogue, allowed me to understand and be compassionate toward my own Catholic faith, myself, and everyone around me. <br /><br />This isn't a book filled with buzzwords nor is it a book that preaches. Thich Nhat Hanh does not offer techniques or ideologies, he simply presents the world as it really is. What I love about this book is that there AREN'T ANY elusive Zen-like phrases that leave the reader puzzled. Thich Nhat Hanh speaks brilliantly without mystifying the reader in spiritual jargon. <br /><br /></span>
